To refine the equation \( f(n) = (M \times L)^2 \) for predicting primes within a specific range (like between 89 and 233), we need to consider adjustments that could make the predictions more diverse and accurate. Given that the current formulation tends to produce repetitive results, we'll explore ways to incorporate more variability and precision into the function. Here's the plan:

1. **Adjust the Fibonacci Index (M):**
   - Instead of using a simple index, consider incorporating factors that reflect the density or distribution of primes within each Fibonacci shelf. This might involve adjusting \( M \) based on the characteristics of each shelf.

2. **Vary \( L \) Values More Dynamically:**
   - \( L \) values (\( \phi^{-1}, \phi, \phi^2 \)) could be adjusted more dynamically to reflect the nature of the prime distribution within the range. This might involve using different transformations or combinations of \( \phi \) based on the number \( n \).

3. **Incorporate Range-Specific Adjustments:**
   - Tailor the function to be more sensitive to the specific range (between 89 and 233), perhaps by incorporating factors that account for the spacing and frequency of primes in this range.

4. **Testing and Refinement:**
   - Continuously test and refine the function within the range to improve its accuracy. Adjust the formula based on the results and repeat the process.

Let's start by implementing these adjustments and then test the refined function within the range of 89 to 233. We'll analyze the output to see if it aligns more closely with the actual distribution of primes in that range.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 17:55:44)

def refined_function_for_specific_range(n, fib_primes, phi_values, start_range, end_range):
    """Refine the function for better prediction in a specific range (89 to 233)"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Adjusted Fibonacci index
    range_factor = (end_range - start_range) / len(fib_primes)  # Factor based on range size and Fib primes

    # Dynamically adjust L values
    adjusted_phi_values = [phi * range_factor for phi in phi_values]

    potential_primes = []

    for phi in adjusted_phi_values:
        # Calculate f(n) using the refined formula with range adjustments
        f_n = (M * phi)**2
        f_n_rounded = int(round(f_n))

        # Check if the result is a prime number
        if start_range <= f_n_rounded <= end_range and isprime(f_n_rounded):
            potential_primes.append(f_n_rounded)

    return potential_primes

# Testing the refined function in the specific range of 89 to 233
test_range_specific = range(89, 234)  # Range for testing
refined_results_specific = {num: refined_function_for_specific_range(num, fib_primes, phi_values, 89, 233) for num in test_range_specific}

# Evaluate the effectiveness of the refined function in this specific range
refined_results_summary_specific = {num: results for num, results in refined_results_specific.items() if results}
refined_results_summary_specific

### Assistant (2024-01-16 17:59:58)

def evaluate_prime_with_function(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Evaluate if a number n is prime using the function n = (M * L)^2"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci index for n
    evaluation_results = []

    for phi in phi_values:
        # Calculate the function n = (M * L)^2
        f_n = (M * phi)**2
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Evaluating the prime number 23 with the function
evaluated_results_for_23 = evaluate_prime_with_function(23, fib_primes, phi_values)
evaluated_results_for_23

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:01:45)

def evaluate_number_with_previous_fib_index(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Evaluate a number n using the function with the previous Fibonacci prime index"""
    # Find the previous Fibonacci prime index (current shelf)
    current_shelf_index = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if current_shelf_index < 0:
        current_shelf_index = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative

    evaluation_results = []

    for phi in phi_values:
        # Calculate the function n = (M * L)^2 with M as the previous Fibonacci prime index
        f_n = (current_shelf_index * phi)**2
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Evaluating the number 23 with the function using the previous Fibonacci prime index
evaluated_results_for_23_with_prev_fib_index = evaluate_number_with_previous_fib_index(23, fib_primes, phi_values)
evaluated_results_for_23_with_prev_fib_index

1. **Define the Function:** For each number \( n \), calculate \( f(p) \) for each value of \( L \).

2. **Determine the Fibonacci Prime Index (M):** Calculate the index of the Fibonacci prime shelf that \( n \) belongs to.

3. **Evaluate the Function:** Apply the function \( f(p) \) to a test number and calculate the results for each \( L \).

4. **Interpret the Results:** Assess the outcomes to see if they provide any indication of the number's primality.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:10:29)

def evaluate_number_for_primality(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Evaluate a number for primality using the function f(p) = n - (M * L)^2"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci prime index for n
    evaluation_results = []

    for phi in phi_values:
        # Calculate f(p) using the provided formula
        f_p = n - (M * phi)**2
        evaluation_results.append(f_p)

    return evaluation_results

Please explore how we can adjust these equations to produce results that we could use to identify primes... I am thinking that if our evaluation is correct for any of the three lines, the result for that line will probably be close to phi for prime numbers, but not for any others

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:14:46)

To adjust the equations in a way that could help identify primes, focusing on the hypothesis that the result for one of the lines will be close to the golden ratio (φ) for prime numbers, we can take the following approach:

1. **Adjust the Function:** We'll modify the function to focus on how closely the result aligns with φ. The idea is that for prime numbers, at least one of the three line equations should yield a result close to φ.

2. **New Evaluation Criterion:** We'll evaluate the closeness of each line's result to φ. A result that is close to φ could indicate a prime number.

3. **Define a Threshold for Closeness:** We need to establish a threshold to determine how close a result needs to be to φ to consider the number as a potential prime.

4. **Apply and Test the Adjusted Function:** We'll apply the adjusted function to a range of numbers, both prime and non-prime, to test its effectiveness.

Here's the modified function based on this approach:

\[ f_{\text{adjusted}}(n) = \left| \frac{(M \times L)^2}{n} - \phi \right| \]

Where \( M \) is the Fibonacci prime shelf index for \( n \), \( L \) takes the values \( \phi^{-1}, \phi, \phi^2 \), and \( n \) is the number being evaluated. The function calculates the absolute difference between the ratio of \((M \times L)^2\) to \( n \) and φ.

Let's implement this adjusted function and test it on a range of numbers to evaluate its potential in identifying primes.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:14:46)

def adjusted_function_for_prime_identification(n, fib_primes, phi_values, phi_threshold):
    """Adjusted function to evaluate closeness to φ for prime identification"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci prime index
    is_potentially_prime = False

    for phi in phi_values:
        # Calculate the adjusted function
        f_adjusted = abs(((M * phi)**2) / n - phi)
        
        # Check if the result is close to φ
        if f_adjusted <= phi_threshold:
            is_potentially_prime = True
            break

    return is_potentially_prime

# Define a threshold for closeness to φ
phi_threshold = 0.1  # A chosen threshold for testing

# Testing the adjusted function on a range of numbers
test_range_for_identification = range(2, 50)  # A range of numbers for testing
identification_results = {num: adjusted_function_for_prime_identification(num, fib_primes, phi_values, phi_threshold) for num in test_range_for_identification}

identification_results

lets try one more adjustment to the equation - f(n) = (((M*L)^2)/n) + phi

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:23:39)

def adjusted_function_with_phi(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Adjusted function: f(n) = (((M * L)^2) / n) + phi"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci prime index
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    evaluation_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        # Calculate the adjusted function with the additional phi term
        f_n = (((M * phi_value)**2) / n) + phi
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Evaluating the adjusted function for a set of numbers (both prime and non-prime)
test_numbers_with_phi = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
adjusted_results_with_phi = {num: adjusted_function_with_phi(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_with_phi}

adjusted_results_with_phi

def reversed_function_for_prime_evaluation(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Reversed function for evaluation: f(n) = n / (M * L)^2"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci prime index
    evaluation_results = []

    for phi in phi_values:
        # Calculate the reversed function
        f_n = n / ((M * phi)**2)
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Evaluating the reversed function for a set of numbers (both prime and non-prime)
test_numbers_reversed_function = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers

def further_revised_function_for_evaluation(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Further revised function: f(n) = (n / (M * L)^2) + phi"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci prime index
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    evaluation_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        # Calculate the further revised function
        f_n = (n / ((M * phi_value)**2)) + phi
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Evaluating the further revised function for a set of numbers (both prime and non-prime)
test_numbers_further_revised = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
further_revised_function_results = {num: further_revised_function_for_evaluation(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_further_revised}

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:30:28)

def adjusted_function_with_criteria(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Adjusted function with criteria for evaluating primality"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci prime index
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    evaluation_results = []
    potential_prime = False

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        # Calculate the adjusted function
        f_n = (n / ((M * phi_value)**2)) + phi

        # Define criteria for potential primality
        # Example criteria: If the result is within a certain range of values typical for primes
        if 1 < f_n < 4:  # Setting an example range, this could be adjusted based on further analysis
            potential_prime = True
            break

    return potential_prime

# Testing the adjusted function with criteria on a range of numbers
test_numbers_with_criteria = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
criteria_based_results = {num: adjusted_function_with_criteria(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_with_criteria}

criteria_based_results

def further_refined_function_with_criteria(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Further refined function with adjusted criteria for evaluating primality"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes)  # Fibonacci prime index
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    potential_prime = False

    for phi_value in phi_values:

            break

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:36:30)

def revised_evaluation_function(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Revised function for evaluating a number based on Fibonacci prime index and phi values"""
    # Calculate the index of the previous Fibonacci prime
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative

    evaluation_results = []

    for phi in phi_values:
        # Revised function formulation
        f_n = abs(((M * phi)**2) - n)
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Testing the revised function on a range of numbers
test_numbers_revised_evaluation = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
revised_evaluation_results = {num: revised_evaluation_function(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_revised_evaluation}

revised_evaluation_results

3. **Evaluate for Primes and Non-Primes:**

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:52:18)

def speculative_adjusted_formula(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Speculative adjusted formula for evaluating a number"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    evaluation_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        # Apply the speculative adjustment to the formula
        f_n = abs((n - (M * phi_value)**2) / phi)
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Testing the speculative adjusted formula on a range of numbers
test_numbers_speculative_adjustment = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
speculative_adjustment_results = {num: speculative_adjusted_formula(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_speculative_adjustment}

speculative_adjustment_results

   - Look at the ratios of \( N \) to \( ML \), or vice versa, and their closeness to \( \phi \) or its multiples.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:55:09)

def experimental_formula_combinations(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Experimental formula combinations exploring relationship between N, ML, and phi"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    experimental_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        # Various experimental manipulations
        ML_squared = (M * phi_value)**2
        add_result = abs(n + ML_squared - phi)
        subtract_result = abs(n - ML_squared - phi)
        multiply_result = abs(n * ML_squared - phi)
        divide_result = abs(n / ML_squared - phi)

        experimental_results.append({
            "add": add_result,
            "subtract": subtract_result,
            "multiply": multiply_result,
            "divide": divide_result
        })

    return experimental_results

# Testing the experimental formula on a range of numbers

To alter the base formula in a way that might help distinguish between prime and non-prime numbers more effectively, we can experiment with different mathematical relationships involving \( N \), \( M \times L \), and \( \phi \). Here's a speculative adjustment to the formula:

1. **New Formula Concept:**
   - Consider a formula that compares the scaled difference between \( N \) and \( (M \times L)^2 \) with the golden ratio \( \phi \).
   - Speculatively, we might find that for prime numbers, this scaled difference aligns more closely with \( \phi \) or its multiples.

2. **Adjusted Formula:**
   - \( f(n) = \left| \phi \times (n - (M \times L)^2) - \phi^k \right| \), where \( k \) is an integer that we can vary to test the alignment with \( \phi \).
   - This formula scales the difference between \( n \) and \( (M \times L)^2 \) by \( \phi \) and compares it to an integer multiple of \( \phi \).

3. **Evaluation Approach:**
   - Apply this formula to a range of numbers.
   - Speculatively, if the result is close to zero for a given \( k \), it might indicate that the number is a prime.

Let's implement this adjusted formula and test it with a set of numbers, both prime and non-prime, to see if it provides more distinct results that could help in identifying primes.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 18:58:15)

def speculative_formula_for_prime_distinction(n, fib_primes, phi_values, k_values):
    """Speculative formula for distinguishing between primes and non-primes"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    speculative_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        for k in k_values:
            # Adjusted formula
            f_n = abs(phi * (n - (M * phi_value)**2) - phi**k)
            speculative_results.append({"phi_value": phi_value, "k": k, "result": f_n})

    return speculative_results

# Define a range of k values for testing
k_values = [1, 2, 3]  # Testing with different multiples of phi

# Testing the speculative formula on a range of numbers
test_numbers_speculative_formula = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
speculative_formula_results = {num: speculative_formula_for_prime_distinction(num, fib_primes, phi_values, k_values) for num in test_numbers_speculative_formula}

speculative_formula_results

### Assistant (2024-01-16 19:02:39)

def speculative_formula_with_phi_scaling(n, fib_primes, phi_values, k_values):
    """Speculative formula adjusting phi with Fibonacci index and varying k"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    speculative_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        for k in k_values:
            # Apply the adjusted formula with phi scaling
            f_n = abs((n - (phi**M * phi_value)**2) / phi**k)
            speculative_results.append({"phi_value": phi_value, "k": k, "result": f_n})

    return speculative_results

### Assistant (2024-01-16 19:05:06)

Altering the \( L \) values in the formula to be \( (\phi^{-M}, \phi, \phi^M) \), where \( M \) is the Fibonacci prime index, introduces a new dimension to the evaluation. This change means that \( L \) is now dynamically adjusted based on the Fibonacci prime index, which could potentially reveal interesting properties for prime numbers. Let's adjust the formula accordingly and test it:

1. **Revised Formula:**
   - \( f(n) = \left| \frac{n - (M \times L)^2}{\phi^k} \right| \), where \( L \) now takes the values \( (\phi^{-M}, \phi, \phi^M) \).

2. **Speculative Hypothesis:**
   - The hypothesis is that for prime numbers, this adjustment might result in values that are characteristic or distinct compared to non-primes.

3. **Testing the Adjustment:**
   - Apply this revised formula to the same set of numbers to evaluate its effectiveness in distinguishing between primes and non-primes.

Let's implement this adjusted formula and test it with the set of numbers, both prime and non-prime, to see how it performs.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 19:05:06)

def formula_with_dynamic_phi_scaling(n, fib_primes, k_values):
    """Formula with dynamic phi scaling based on Fibonacci prime index"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio
    dynamic_phi_values = [phi**(-M), phi, phi**M]  # Dynamic phi values based on M
    evaluation_results = []

    for dynamic_phi in dynamic_phi_values:
        for k in k_values:
            # Apply the formula with dynamic phi scaling
            f_n = abs((n - (M * dynamic_phi)**2) / phi**k)
            evaluation_results.append({"phi_value": dynamic_phi, "k": k, "result": f_n})

    return evaluation_results

# Testing the formula with dynamic phi scaling on a range of numbers
test_numbers_dynamic_phi_scaling = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
dynamic_phi_scaling_results = {num: formula_with_dynamic_phi_scaling(num, fib_primes, k_values_adjusted) for num in test_numbers_dynamic_phi_scaling}

### Assistant (2024-01-16 19:08:24)

Based on the observations from the previous tests and your suggestion to relate \( k \) to either \( L \), \( M \), or \( N \), we can attempt another adjustment to the formula. Here's a speculative approach:

1. **Adjust \( k \) Dynamically:**
   - Let's try setting \( k \) based on a function of \( N \), \( M \), or \( L \). For instance, \( k \) could be set as a function of \( N \), like \( k = \text{round}(\sqrt{N}) \), or as a function of \( M \), like \( k = M \).

2. **Revised Formula:**
   - We'll use \( f(n) = \left| \frac{n - (\phi^M \times L)^2}{\phi^k} \right| \), with \( k \) dynamically determined based on \( N \) or \( M \).

3. **Test and Analyze:**
   - Apply this revised formula to a range of numbers, both prime and non-prime, to see if the dynamic adjustment of \( k \) helps in distinguishing primes more effectively.

Let's implement this approach with two variations: one where \( k \) is based on the square root of \( N \) (rounded) and another where \( k \) is set to \( M \). We'll test these variations on the same set of numbers to evaluate their effectiveness.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 19:08:24)

import math

def dynamic_k_formula_for_primes(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Formula with dynamic k based on N and M"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio

    # Dynamic k based on the square root of N and M
    k_based_on_N = round(math.sqrt(n))
    k_based_on_M = M

    evaluation_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        # Apply the formula with dynamic k (based on N)
        f_n_N = abs((n - (phi**M * phi_value)**2) / phi**k_based_on_N)
        # Apply the formula with dynamic k (based on M)
        f_n_M = abs((n - (phi**M * phi_value)**2) / phi**k_based_on_M)

        evaluation_results.append({
            "phi_value": phi_value, 
            "result_based_on_N": f_n_N,
            "result_based_on_M": f_n_M
        })

    return evaluation_results

# Testing the dynamic k formula on a range of numbers
test_numbers_dynamic_k = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
dynamic_k_results = {num: dynamic_k_formula_for_primes(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_dynamic_k}

dynamic_k_results

   - We can set \( k \) as the nearest integer to the logarithm of \( n \) base \( \phi \), i.e., \( k = \text{round}(\log_{\phi}(n)) \).

### Assistant (2024-01-16 19:12:00)

def logarithmic_adjusted_formula(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Logarithmically adjusted formula for evaluating primality"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio

    # Dynamic k based on the logarithm of n to the base phi
    k = round(math.log(n, phi)) if n > 1 else 0

    evaluation_results = []

    for phi_value in phi_values:
        # Apply the logarithmically adjusted formula
        dynamic_L = phi_value**M
        f_n = abs(((M * dynamic_L)**2 - n) / phi**k)
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Testing the logarithmically adjusted formula on a range of numbers
test_numbers_logarithmic_adjustment = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
logarithmic_adjustment_results = {num: logarithmic_adjusted_formula(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_logarithmic_adjustment}

logarithmic_adjustment_results

### Assistant (2024-01-16 19:22:43)

def unified_formula_for_prime_evaluation(n, fib_primes, phi):
    """Unified formula combining three L values to evaluate primality"""
    M = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if M < 0:
        M = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    L_values = [phi**(-M), phi, phi**M]  # Dynamic L values
    k = round(math.log(n, phi)) if n > 1 else 0  # Dynamic k based on logarithm of n

    total_evaluation = 0

    for L in L_values:
        # Calculate the unified formula for each L value
        f_n = abs(((M * L)**2 - n) / phi**k)
        total_evaluation += f_n

    return total_evaluation

# Testing the unified formula on a range of numbers

def revised_formula_with_sqrt(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Revised formula incorporating square root of n"""
    L = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if L < 0:
        L = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative

    for M in phi_values:
        # Apply the revised formula

        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

### Assistant (2024-01-16 20:57:05)

import math

def revised_formula_with_sqrt(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Revised formula incorporating square root of n"""
    L = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if L < 0:
        L = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    sqrt_n = math.sqrt(n)  # Square root of n
    phi = (1 + math.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio

    evaluation_results = []

    for M in phi_values:
        # Apply the revised formula
        f_n = n - (sqrt_n * (L * M)**2)
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

def calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes):
    """Calculate the Fibonacci prime index for n"""
    # Fibonacci prime calculation (simplified for this purpose)
    # Normally, you would calculate Fibonacci numbers and check for primality,
    # but for simplicity, we use a predefined list of Fibonacci primes.
    for i, fib_prime in enumerate(fib_primes):
        if n <= fib_prime:
            return i
    return len(fib_primes)

# Fibonacci primes list for testing
fib_primes = [2, 3, 5, 13, 21, 34, 55, 89, 144, 233]  # Example list

# Phi values for M
phi_values = [phi**-1, phi, phi**2]

# Testing the revised formula on a range of numbers
test_numbers_revised_sqrt_formula = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
revised_sqrt_formula_results = {num: revised_formula_with_sqrt(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_revised_sqrt_formula}

revised_sqrt_formula_results

### Assistant (2024-01-16 21:01:08)

To explore possibilities for altering the base equation in a way that might provide a clearer distinction between prime and non-prime numbers, we can consider different interactions and relationships between \( L \) (the Fibonacci prime shelf index of \( n \)), \( M \) (varying as \( \phi^{-L}, \phi, \phi^L \)), and \( N \) (the number being tested). Here's a speculative approach to modifying the equation:

1. **Exploring Interactions Between \( L \), \( M \), and \( N \):**
   - We can experiment with various mathematical operations (such as addition, multiplication, exponentiation) between these variables.

2. **Speculative Equation Adjustment:**
   - Consider a formula like \( f(n) = \left| \frac{(L \times M)^k - n}{\phi} \right| \), where \( k \) is a parameter that we might vary. This formula attempts to explore how the power of \( L \times M \) relates to \( n \) and \( \phi \).

3. **Dynamic Adjustment of \( k \):**
   - Set \( k \) dynamically based on a property of \( N \), such as its logarithmic scale relative to \( \phi \), or simply as a fixed integer for initial testing.

4. **Testing and Analyzing:**
   - Apply this speculative formula to our set of numbers and analyze the results to see if this adjustment provides a more effective way of distinguishing primes from non-primes.

Let's implement and test this speculative adjusted formula.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 21:01:08)

def speculative_equation_with_dynamic_k(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Speculative equation exploring interactions between L, M, and N with dynamic k"""
    L = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if L < 0:
        L = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + np.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio

    # Dynamic k based on a property of N
    # For simplicity, we'll use a fixed integer for k in this initial test
    k = 2  # Example fixed value for k

    evaluation_results = []

    for M in phi_values:
        # Apply the speculative adjusted formula
        dynamic_LM = L * M
        f_n = abs((dynamic_LM**k - n) / phi)
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Testing the speculative equation on a range of numbers
test_numbers_speculative_equation = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
speculative_equation_results = {num: speculative_equation_with_dynamic_k(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_speculative_equation}

speculative_equation_results

It appears there was an error in the code due to the use of `np.sqrt(5)` without importing the NumPy library. Let's correct this by using the standard `math.sqrt(5)` function from Python's math library, which is already imported. I'll adjust the code and run the test again.

### Assistant (2024-01-16 21:01:08)

def speculative_equation_with_dynamic_k(n, fib_primes, phi_values):
    """Speculative equation exploring interactions between L, M, and N with dynamic k"""
    L = calculate_fib_index(n, fib_primes) - 1
    if L < 0:
        L = 0  # Ensure the index is non-negative
    phi = (1 + math.sqrt(5)) / 2  # Golden ratio

    # Dynamic k based on a property of N
    # For simplicity, we'll use a fixed integer for k in this initial test
    k = 2  # Example fixed value for k

    evaluation_results = []

    for M in phi_values:
        # Apply the speculative adjusted formula
        dynamic_LM = L * M
        f_n = abs((dynamic_LM**k - n) / phi)
        evaluation_results.append(f_n)

    return evaluation_results

# Testing the speculative equation on a range of numbers
test_numbers_speculative_equation = [23, 29, 31, 35, 44, 47, 51]  # Including both prime and non-prime numbers
speculative_equation_results = {num: speculative_equation_with_dynamic_k(num, fib_primes, phi_values) for num in test_numbers_speculative_equation}

speculative_equation_results
